But in those who have hot abscesses in the mouth or throat or both ears, when the disease is not in the windpipe, it is fitting to use the cutting of the epiglottis to avoid the loss which is caused by suffocation.
Therefore it is fitting when we want this, that we cut the epiglottis below three circles of the circles of the epiglottis, or four with a small incision for the width in that which is between two circles by quantity, so that the cut is in the membrane, not in the cartilage, and this place is suitable for cutting, because it is devoid of flesh and its blood vessels are far away.
And if the physician is fearful, it is fitting then that he stretch the skin of the throat with a hook, and afterwards split the skin until he reaches the canal, but avoid the blood vessels if you see any of them.
And afterwards cut the membrane as we have recounted; and it is indicated above the cut of the canal by the phlegm which has come out of it with that which is disrupted from it and by the loss of voice.
And leave the wound open for some time.
Therefore when the time has passed in which perforation is feared, bring together the two lips of the skin of the wound, and sew it alone without the cartilage.
And afterwards administer medicines that make flesh grow until it is healed.
And Albucasis said that the summary of the discourse which we have recounted, the explanation is nothing but that you see that some of these abscesses have already blocked the throat of the patient, and the patient has come to the point of death, and his breath is cut off, and some go to cut the epiglottis so that the patient may breathe over the place of the wound by some respiration, and be saved from death.
And for this they commanded to leave the wound open until the malignancy of the disease is consumed; and its malignancy is for three days; and then they commanded to sew the wound, and cure it until it is healed.
And what I have seen for myself, is that a servant took a knife and put it in her throat and cut with it a part of the windpipe, and I was called to the cure of her, and I found the moaning as is the moaning of the dying, and I uncovered the wound and found the blood which had come out of the wound little.
Therefore I confessed that she had not cut a vein or windpipe, and the air was coming out of the wound, and I cured it until it was healed.
And nothing happened to the servant except hoarseness in the voice, and after some days she returned to improvement of her conditions.
And now I say that in the cutting of the epiglottis there is no fear.
Chapter 44.
On cutting above an abscess which occurs in the throat outside, and is called hernia of the throat.
This abscess named hernia of the throat is a large abscess according to the color of the body, and is common in women.
And it is according to two manners, for it is either natural or accidental.
And in the natural there is no means of curing.
And the accidental is according to two manners of which one is similar to fatty nodes, and the other manner is similar to an abscess which is made by knotting of an artery, and in that there is fear. And it is not fitting that presumption be made to it with iron except in that which is small. And you test it and investigate it with the finger, and if you find it similar to a fatty node, and it is not suspended with any of the veins, then you cut it just like the nodes, and extract it with that which contains it of the skin and sac; and if not, then all its being is examined, and afterwards cure the place with that which is fitting for curing until it is healed.
Chapter 45.
On the incision of the types of nodes.
There are many types of nodes and I have already mentioned all their types in the division.
And it is appropriate that I recount here the difference between node and exitura as it causes doubt.
So I say that with exitura there is heat and fever and vehement pains until the ebullition of the superfluity is calmed; and putrefaction is complete when the fever, pain and heat cease.
But with a node there is no heat nor fever nor pain, and it contains that ciphac leon which is in its own sac.
And it is according to the color of the body, and its beginning is like a chickpea and it is made thus as it grows, be it major or minor, and they are of two types, for they are either fatty and contain humidity, and the colors of the humidity are many, as I said in the division.
So it is appropriate, when you come to the cure of a node, that you examine it and investigate it at the beginning with an instrument which is called intromes, as its form will come in the chapter which is after this one.
And it is a manner of investigation of apostemas and of all nodes, and it is that you take this instrument and introduce it in the most humid place which you find in the apostema, and you will revolve your fingers with it little by little until you know that the instrument has already penetrated the skin.
And after, move your hand according to the measure of the size of the apostema, and then extract the intromes and consider what has come out in its trace.
And if the running humidity is expelled, of whatever color it may be, then you incise it with a superficial incision as I have said in the other apostemas.
And if no humidity comes out of the trace of the intromes, then know that it is fatty.
And dry over it with an incision having the form of a cross according to this form: as I have taught you, and suspend it with hooks, and skin the hide from all parts with ease, and keep the skin or sac, if you can, over it and extract that sanies with the node.
But if it is broken in the operation, it is not possible to extract it healthy, and this happens many times, and then you extract it in pieces until nothing remains of it.
For if any of it remains, little or much, the node returns according to the greater part.
And if you see that some small part of it remains, then complete the wound with some sharp corrosive powders and tighten the wound, and place on it what calms a hot apostema, and cure it with the other cure until it is healed.
And if it is a large node, then you sew its two lips and cure it with what incarnates.
But if a pulsating vein is contrary to it, or non-pulsating, then you hasten and fill the place with ground vitriol and leave it tight for two days or for three until the wound rots and the ebullition of the blood rests; and after return to incise what remains of the node.

Chapter 47.
On the treatment of men's breasts which resemble those of women.
Sometimes the breasts of some men are swollen towards the completion of sleep when they begin to be hairy, and afterwards the breasts are swollen, and the breasts resemble those of women, and remain swollen, ugly.
And for one who dislikes this, it is appropriate to cut them with a lunar incision according to this form, from the line of B to the line of G, and afterwards skin all the thickness, and afterwards fill the wound with incarnative medicine, and afterwards join the two lips of the wound with suture, and treat that until it is healed.
But if the breast declines to the lower parts and is softened by its magnitude as happens to women, then it should be split in its two upper sides, with two incisions resembling a lunar figure, of which each is contained in the other towards the end of each, until the major line contains the minor according to this form from the line of B and the line of G. And afterwards skin the hide which is between two lips of the wound, and remove the fat, and administer what we have said about the suture and the powders that which is necessary in the treatment until it is healed.
And if you do not complete the incision of what should be cut due to the restlessness of the patient, and due to blood flow, then it is appropriate that you fill the wound with cotton submerged in corrosive ointment and leave that until it corrodes what remains of the fat, and afterwards treat that until it is healed.
Chapter 48.
On the perforation of abscesses that come under the armpit.
These abscesses that come under the armpit are of the species of scrofula, hard, which contain a skin that is like a sac.
And of these, some contain fluids; and those that contain fluids should be incised with a lunar section according to this figure: from line G to line B. And when all that is in the abscess of pus is evacuated, then you fill it with old cotton and leave it until the next day.
And after the cotton is removed, it should be treated with a suitable ointment for this, until it is healed.
And if the abscess is of the species of nodes, and of scrofula, then you cut over it as we have said in the section on scrofula equally.
But if the wound is extended so that pus comes out, then administer cautery to it as we have said before.
Chapter 49.
On the incision of abscesses that occur by artery or by vein.
When an artery is ruptured, and the skin is consolidated which is over it, then many times an abscess occurs. And the signs by which it is known that inflammation and abscess are by the artery or by vein: for when the abscess is by artery it is long gathered in the depth of the body; and when you press the abscess with your fingers, you feel in it as if there is a whistle.
And that which is by vein is round to the manifest of the body.
And incision on this abscess is an error, and especially in that which is under the armpits, and in the groins, and in the neck, and in many places of the body; and it is very large, so it is appropriate that its cure with iron be avoided, and that which is in the extremities, or in the head, should be avoided.
But on that which is of them by inflammation of the orifice of the artery, cut in the skin a section in the length; and after open the section with hooks and after the artery, and deliver from the tunics until it is uncovered.
And after put a needle on it and make it penetrate to the other side, and tighten the artery with double thread in two places, — which thing I taught you in extraction of two arteries which are in the temples.
And after puncture the place which is between two ligaments with a spatula until all the blood that is in it comes out, and the abscess is dissolved.
And after administer treatment in which pus is generated until the ligaments fall; and after cure it with ointments suitable for this until it is healed.
And if it is an abscess by section of vein, then it is appropriate that you hold with your hand what is possible for you of the abscess with the skin, and after introduce the needle under the place which you have held under your hand, and make it penetrate; and let there be in it double thread until you extract it from the other side, and after tie the abscess with good binding as I have told you in the binding of grape of two parts with two extremities of the thread.
But if you fear that we extract the thread, then introduce the thread with that needle under all the abscess towards the incision of the first needle, and tighten your threads in four places.
After dry the abscess in the middle place of it until when what is in it has come out, then you cut the superfluity of the skin, and leave that which of it is bound.
And after place on it a compress which you have submerged in wine and oil, and after administer the treatment which is made with poultices and ointments until it is healed.
Chapter 50 on the aposteme which occurs due to twisting of nerves.
Just as aposteme occurs in arteries and veins, similarly aposteme occurs in the nerves when there is percussion or excessive work, and similar causes.
And it is mostly made in the places of the arms or the heel, or in any place where the joints are moved.
And it is a serious aposteme, and it resembles the color of the rest of the body, and in most cases it is without pain and when it is tightly pressed, the patient feels a numbness-like sensation.
And the aposteme is not gathered in the depths of the body, so it is under the skin, and it moves to all parts and does not go to the front or back parts.
Therefore, those that are in the joints should not be invaded with iron, because contraction would easily occur.
But that which is on the head or on the forehead, cut the skin with a spatula. But if the aposteme is small, then hold it with forceps and cut it out from the root.
And if it is large, then you suspend it with a hook, and flay it, and then remove it; and close the wound with sutures, and treat it until it is healed.
Chapter 51.
On cutting the aposteme which occurs from growths that occur on the belly.
It happens to some men many times in their bellies and in other parts of their bodies growths which are called fungal because of their similarity to mushrooms, of which the root is thin and the head is large; and their edges are turned, and some are small, and some are very enlarged.
And I have seen one, and in its belly were two growths which were more like mushrooms, and there was no difference between those white ones, with a small root.
And their edges were inverted and split, and moisture ran from it all the time.
So I cut them and found in one a weight of about 18 ounces and the other about 6 ounces.
And the operation in cutting them is that you consider then if the patient is moist, and the color of the growth is white, moist, with a thin root; then you cut it with a broad spatula, and have cauteries in the fire in your presence, because often after cutting it much blood is expelled; and if the blood overcomes you, cauterize it.
And if you see the patient fearful and timid, beware of cutting with iron; but then take newly made lead wire, and tighten the growth with it, the manner of which is that which we have said; and leave it for two days.
And afterwards add to the tightening of the lead wire; so, do not cease to tighten the lead many times on the growth, until it is cut off and falls by itself without effort.
But if the growth has a thick root, then in cutting it there is some cause for concern and fear, especially in that which is on the belly.
But it is possible that you cut half of it, and afterwards cauterize it so that it does not return.
And afterwards treat it until the wound is healed.
And beware that you do not presume to cut a growth which is of dark color, of little feeling, of ugly appearance, because that is almost cancerous.
And I will come with a reminder of cancer after this.
Chapter 52
On the treatment of swelling of the navel.
Swelling of the navel is caused by many things: by fissures in the abdominal wall, from which the membrane or intestine protrudes as in other ruptures; by blood flowing from a vein or artery as mentioned before, or by trapped gas.
But if it's due to a fissure in the abdominal wall and protrusion of the membrane, then the color of the swelling is similar to the body's color; it's soft without pain, and appears in different positions. And if it's due to intestinal protrusion, then its position varies more than what we've described, and when you press it with your fingers it disappears, then returns; it's often accompanied by sound, and is greatly enlarged by bathing and strenuous work.
But if it's due to fluid, then it's soft and doesn't disappear when you press with your hand, nor is it constrained or enlarged.
And if it's due to blood, then with these signs the swelling appears to be darkening.
But if it's due to flesh growth, then the swelling is serious, large and hard, and is fixed in one place.
But if it's due to gas, then touching it feels soft.
The procedure is to consider whether the navel swelling is due to arterial or venous blood, or gas; then it's advisable to avoid treating it, because it's dangerous as I've taught you in the chapter about swellings caused by arteries and veins.
If the navel swelling is due to intestine or membrane, then you should instruct the patient to hold their breath and lie stretched out; then mark around the entire navel with a probe, and then tell them to lie face up between your hands on their back, and then encircle the navel area you marked with a broad spatula; then extend half of the swelling to the upper parts with a large hook; and then tie around it with strong thread or silk in a proper tying manner.
Then open the middle of the swelling extended over the tie and insert your finger into that opening and search for the intestine; if you've found it and secured it with the tie, then you extract it carefully and push the intestine into the inner parts of the belly.
And if you've found the membrane, then take it with a hook; and cut away the excess parts of it.
But if you encounter an artery or vein, then carefully go around it, and then return to your operation; and take two needles and put two strong threads in them and insert the two needles into the circle you've made around the swelling in the shape of a cross, which you should make penetrate; and then tighten the swelling in four parts over the needles.
And if you want, remove the needles and leave the place until the extended flesh rots and falls off by itself; or cut it when it's thinned and rotting, and then treat it with appropriate ointments until it's healed.
And if the navel swelling is from flesh grown there or from fluid, then you should hollow out the swelling as we've said and remove the blood or fluid which you find in it, and then treat it with what's appropriate and consolidate the area.
Chapter 53
On the treatment of cancer.
We have already spoken, in the division, of the type of cancer and in what manner it is treated with medicines, and that treatment with iron should be avoided so that it does not become ulcerated; and we have spoken of cancer generated in the womb and caution in treating it.
And the ancients said that sometimes cancer is in a place where it is possible to eradicate it, such as cancer which is in the breasts or in the thigh and similar parts of the body allocated to extract all of it, and especially when it is beginning small.
But when it is old and large, it is not advisable that you attempt it, for I have not been able to cure anyone of it nor have I seen another do so, nor that it has come to that.
And the operation on it when it is located as we have said, is that you proceed and leave the patient and purge the black bile sometimes, and afterwards bleed them, if manifest repletion is found.
And afterwards prepare the patient with preparation in which it is placed with operation, and afterwards throw into the hole hooks which are suitable for that; and afterwards hollow out from all sides with the skin according to good examination until no part of its roots remains. And let the blood run, and do not cut it lightly, and press the places, and wipe away the thick blood all with your hand or with an instrument with which it is possible for you from the instruments.
But if cutting a vein or artery causes you difficulty with thick blood, then cauterize it until the blood flow has ceased, and afterwards treat it with the other treatment until it is healed.
Chapter 54
On the treatment of dropsy.
We have already recounted, in the division, the types of water dropsy, and the signs of each type, of treating it with medicines.
And that which is treated with iron is only the species of ascites alone, and the species of tympanites nor the species of anasarca should not be approached with iron, for that is fatal.
And when you have already treated this species of tympanitic dropsy with medicines and your medication does not work, then consider, for if weakness has already come to the patient, or they have another illness besides dropsy, such as if they have a cough or stomach ache and similar to those, then be careful not to treat them with iron, for there is fear about that.
But if you see the patient with abundant strength, and they have no other illness but dropsy only, and neither a child nor old, then the manner of operating on them is that you raise the patient between your hands, and the minister afterwards presses their belly with his hand, pushing the water to the lower part of the pubic area, and afterwards take a spiny spatula according to this form:
Let it be long with two sharp parts, with a sharp end like a spatula; but let there be in it some shortness little by little, so that in operating with it you do not pass through to the intestine, and injure it.
And afterwards consider if the generation of dropsy is from the part of the intestines, for then it is advisable that you with the incision move away from the navel by the quantity of three fingers to the lower parts, in the right of it above the pubic area.
But if the generation of dropsy is by illness of the liver, then let your incision be to the left of the navel by three fingers.
And if its generation is by the spleen, then let your incision be on the right side.
And it is not advisable that your incision be on the side on which the patient wants to lie so that the superfluities do not run to that weak place.
And afterwards perforate with the instrument all the skin, and afterwards introduce into that incision, and raise your hand with the spatula between the skin and the peritoneum, and you flay it; and let the quantity be of a fingernail or thereabouts.
And afterwards pierce the abdomen until you reach the empty space at the location, which is the place of the water. And after extracting that, introduce an instrument of which this is the form: and it is similar to a thin silver tube; it is made of silver or copper or brass, which at its lower part has a small hole, and on its sides are three holes: two on one side and one on the other side; and its extremity is cut in the manner of a pen, as you see:
And at its upper extremity is a ring, for when the instrument reaches the water, then it immediately descends over the instrument, thus evacuating half the quantity of water in an hour, for if you evacuate more than is suitable in an hour, the patient very easily dies by dissolution of his animal spirit, or syncope occurs which is close to death.
But evacuate it according to the quantity of his strength and according to what the patient's condition indicates to you of the strength of his pulse and his wellbeing.
And after extracting the instrument, the water is retained which is because it is immediately held by the skin which retains the hole that is above the abdomen of which I have told you to pierce in that manner.
And afterwards repeat the instrument the next day if you see the patient tolerating it, and extract a small quantity of water, and do this for some days with caution, and guard yourself from error until only a little water remains.
But if you fear for the patient, and leave a large quantity of water, then treat him with burial in warm sand, and much sweating in a bath, and in the sun waiting for a long time; and treat him with drying medicines until he is healed.
And cauterize over the stomach, and the spleen and the liver after the extraction of the water, as I have recounted in what has preceded.
Chapter 55.
On the treatment of infants who are born with the places of urine not perforated.
Sometimes some of the infants come out of their mother's womb and the head of their urethra is not perforated (or the hole is narrow or not in its place).

And afterwards place in the hole a thin lead nail and tie it, and keep it for three days or four.
And when he wants to urinate, let it be removed and let him urinate; and afterwards return it.

But he whose hole is narrow should be treated with a lead nail, as we have said, for many days until it is widened.
But those in whom the hole is not in its place, are injured, which is because of those, the one who is born and the hole is towards the end of the head of the penis so that he cannot urinate to the inner parts, until he raises the penis with his hand to the upper parts; and there is no generation for him, because the sperm cannot reach the mother in a straight line, and it is a very ugly disease.
And the manner of operation on him is that the patient be laid on his back, and afterwards extend the head of his penis with your left hand with vehement extraction, and cut the head of the penis from the place of the foreskin with a sharp blade, as is the cutting of a pen, or that you shave some part of it, so that its middle comes to resemble the head of the penis and that the hole falls in the middle place as is suitable.
And guard yourself in your operation from blood flow, for many times this happens; and apply to him with that which stops the blood, and treat the wound until it is healed.
Chapter 56.
About a growth which occurs on the foreskin at the head of the penis, and about corruption and blackening and adhesion of the foreskin to the head of the penis.
Many times this growth occurs on the penis and it is a prominence of ugly flesh.

But if the growth is on the foreskin of the head of the uncircumcised penis, and one part of the growth is inside the foreskin and the other part is outside, then it is suitable that you remove the growth which is inside at the beginning until it is consolidated; and then you treat that outside, because when you treat that together with the foreskin, it is not assured that it will not be cut.
And likewise it happens in the genitals and in the foreskin blackening and corruption, then it is suitable that you remove all that which is already blackened and which is about to corrupt or which is already corrupted; and afterwards apply to that after this with honey, which is mixed with flour of pomegranate bark and ground and sifted vetch.
And afterwards treat that with the other treatment until it is healed.
But if blood flow occurs, then administer lunar cautery according to this form:
for beneficial cautery is for two conditions together, that is for blood flow and for the wound when it is corrupted.
And if the head of the penis is corroded and is completely destroyed at the time, then it is suitable that you insert a lead tube into the opening of the foreskin so that the patient can urinate through it.
In the adhesion of the foreskin to the head of the penis (and this adhesion only happens in one whose foreskin is healthy, and on which circumcision is not required; and when adhesion happens due to a wound or abscess) it is suitable that you separate with a blunt spatula until the bond is dissolved and the head of the penis is freed from all parts.
And if it is difficult to separate these precisely, then it is suitable that you scrape with a spatula something from the head of the penis and from the foreskin, and this is because the foreskin, when it is thin, is very easily perforated due to its thinness.
And afterwards separate between the foreskin and the head of the penis with a thin linen cloth, which has been moistened in cold water so that they do not adhere again.
And afterwards let it be treated with astringent wine until it is healed.
Chapter 57.
About the cleansing of children and the treatment of what happens to them from circumcision.
Circumcision is not a solution of continuity like other wounds: but however as it is of our operation and of our will, and its use is primarily in children, it is necessary that we assign in it the best operation and easiest way leading to health.
Therefore I say that the ancients did not describe circumcision in any of their books, because they do not use it in their laws, and it is only because we have acquired it through experiment, which is that I have found the majority of craftsmen and barbers using circumcision and cleansing with a razor and with forceps; and they use tying with thread and cutting with the fingernail.
And I have already tried all these methods and did not find better cleansing with scissors, with tying with thread than in cleansing with the fingernail, because many times the upper skin escapes, because the skin of the foreskin has two layers, and the lower layer remains, and very easily it is forced to another incision and secure pain. And with cleansing which is done by alphecati, and is digital, which cobblers use, the incision of the extremity of the male member is not secured, for it easily enters into its hole.
But in the operation with a nail, iron easily obeys and corrupts your operation. And the foreskin of the child is naturally short, and often born in such a way that it has no need of cleansing, and I have seen this.
But of the cleansing that is done with scissors and bindings with thread, the goodness, experiment revealed to me, for the scissors are of proportional incision, because the sharpness that is above is like the sharpness that is below; and thus when you press your hand they are proportioned two sharpnesses, and they cut according to a comparison at one time; and compression of the thread is made with a figure containing the foreskin of the penis from all parts, with which no error falls at all.
And the manner of the first operation is that you make the child stay, especially if he is one of those who understand a little, that you do nothing but tie the thread on his penis only, and leave it until the next day.
And afterward make him rejoice in every way that is possible to you from what his intelligence receives. And afterward make him stay between your hands standing prepared, and not sitting; and hide the scissors in your hand or under your foot, so that the child does not see them nor any other of the instruments.
And afterward introduce your hand to his penis and blow on the foreskin, and pull it until the head of the penis has come out, and afterward clean it of what is gathered on it of dirt.
The form of the scissors for cleansing, this is the form:
Let one extremity be non-cutting and the other be cutting, that the branch of the nail not be out, and let the length of the two sharpnesses be like the length of two handles equally.
But the error in cleansing is that the inner foreskin very easily escapes whole, or part of it towards the incision.
Therefore it is necessary that you extend it from your time with your nail before the swelling of the place and that you cut it according to equality.
And if you cannot hold it with your nail, then extract it with a hook and cut it.
But if three days have passed, and what is swollen remains under the penis swollen, then you leave that until the hot swelling has subsided, and skin it with ease, and cut it according to what is prepared for you.
And guard yourself from the head of the penis, for that will not harm it.
And then cure it with that which consolidates the wound of the powders which we have recounted in the treatise on powders.
And if it is cut of the foreskin over measure, and obeys the upper parts, that does not harm it.
And moreover cure it with what we have said until it is healed.
Chapter 58.
On the treatment of urine retained in the bladder.
Retention of urine in the bladder is caused by blockage due to stone, congealed blood, pus, or flesh growth, and similar to those we have mentioned in the types of treatments in the division.
And if it is not dissolved with what we have said and the condition becomes severe for the patient, then it is necessary to administer extraction with an instrument which is called a syringe, of which this is the form: Let it be of silver and be a subtle hollow tube, like the quill of a bird’s feather with the subtlety of a long ray in the likeness of a palm and a half, to which is a thin tube at its head.
And the manner of the urine's exit through it is that you take the doubled thread and tie wool or cotton at its extremity with a good binding; and insert the ends of the thread in the lower part of the syringe, and cut with scissors if any part of the wool is superfluous, but insert it into the tube with force. And then anoint the syringe with butter and egg white.
And make the patient sit on the chair, and bathe his bladder and penis with moist oils, olive oil and rose water.
And then insert the syringe gently until it reaches the root of the penis; and then bend the penis upwards towards the navel; and then push the syringe inside it; and then push it until it reaches the bladder, and the patient feels it has reached the empty space, and this is not done according to this order, except for the passage which goes in a tortuous way.
And then extend the thread with the wool little by little, for the urine follows the wool.
Then extract it and make urine for treatment, and use the syringe, do not cease to do this and use the syringe until the bladder is evacuated and the patient finds relief.

Chapter 60.
On the extraction of stone.
We have already spoken about the division of types of stone and their treatment with medicines, and the difference between stone formed in the kidneys and stone formed in the bladder, and their signs.
And we have spoken about the stone in which operation by hand and cutting is necessary.
And the stone formed in the bladder is properly that which is fixed in the bladder.
And I am narrating that with clear explanation and brevity.
So I say that stone formed in the bladder mostly comes to children; and among its signs is that the urine that comes out of the bladder is similar to water in its thinness, and sand appears in it; and the patient rubs his penis, and often hangs, and then is erected; and with that the anus comes out in many of them.
And the healing of children from that is easy until they have reached 14 years; and treatment is difficult in old men. But in young men it is intermediate because it is between those.
And for one whose stone is larger the treatment is easier; And if it is small, it is the opposite to that.
So when we come to the treatment of that, it is appropriate at the beginning of it that we cleanse the patient with an enema which extracts all the excrement which is in his intestines; because that excrement sometimes prevents the discovery of the stone during the examination of it.
And then let the patient be taken by his feet and shaken and moved downwards so that the stone descends to the bottom of the bladder, or that it jumps from a high place sometimes.
And then make him sit prepared between your hands, and his hands should be under his thighs, so that the whole bladder is made to incline to the lower parts.
And then examine it and all of it from outside.
So if you feel the stone in the space, then you hurry at once with cutting over it.
And if it doesn't fall completely under your touch, then it is appropriate that you anoint with oil your index finger of the left hand, if the patient is a child, or the middle finger if he is a grown young man, and insert that in his anus. And search for the stone until it is under your finger. And turn it little by little until the neck of the bladder.
And then press on it with your finger, and expel it to the outer parts towards the place from which you make the cut.
And command the minister to press the bladder with his hand; and command another minister to extend the genitals to the upper parts with his right hand, and with his other hand to move the skin which is below the genitals, in part of the place where the incision is made.
And after that, introduce a well-cutting spatula of which this is its form: and cut with it that which is between the anus and the genitals, not in the middle place, but to the side of the left thigh; and let the incision be over that stone and your finger be in the anus, and let a transverse incision be made, so that the outer incision is wide and the inner narrow according to the quantity that the removal of the stone is possible to it, and no greater, for your finger which is in the anus very easily compresses the stone towards the incision, and it is expelled without difficulty.
And know that of the stone there is some which have angles and edges, because of which its exit is made difficult.
And of that, it is like a lion similar to an acorn, and it is round, and its exit is made easily.
Therefore if it is one which has angles and edges, add to the fissure.
And if it is not expelled thus, then it is necessary that you contrive upon it, or that you press upon it with a decent gesture, the extremity of which should be like a file with which you press upon the stone, and it does not escape from it; or that you introduce below it a subtle instrument with a curved extremity.
But if you cannot do this, then you enlarge the hole a little, and if you see a flow of blood, cut it off by pressing it with ground vitriol.
But if there is more than one stone, then at the beginning you push the hand to the mouth of the bladder, and after cut over it; and after push a little after that; and do similarly if there are many more than two.
And if it is a very large stone, then it is ignorance that you cut it with a large incision, for one of two things happens to the patient: either he dies or continuous urine leakage befalls him, because the place is not completely consolidated.
But administer its expulsion until it is expelled, or contrive in breaking it with forceps until you extract it in pieces.
Therefore when you will have completed your operation, then fill the wound with incense of aloe and dragon's blood, and tighten it. And place over it a cloth soaked in oil and wine, or in rose oil and cold water, so that hot swelling may be reduced.
And after lay the patient on his back, and do not untie the bandage until the third day.
And when you have untied it, bathe the place with water and much oil, and after treat it with diafinicon ointment and diabazilicon ointment until it is healed.
But if in the wound there occurs hot swelling, burning and corrosive, and similar to that as if the blood is congealed in the bladder, and because of it the urine is prohibited (and this is known by the exit of blood with urine), then introduce your finger into the wound and extract that blood, for if it remains it provokes the bladder to corruption of the bladder and putrefaction of it.
And after wash the wound with vinegar, water and salt, and with opposition to every kind, with that which is suitable to it of the treatment until it is healed.
It is necessary during the hours of all the treatment that you bind both thighs and apply the medicines which are placed on the location.
And if the stone is small and is in the passage of the penis, and is stuck in it, and likewise urine is prohibited, then cure that with what I recount before you proceed to cutting, because too often for this cure you are accused of cutting; and I have already tested this, and it is that you take an iron perforator alfelt, of which this is the form of it:
of triangular extremity, sharp, fixed in wood.
And after take thread, and tie with that the penis below the stone so that it does not return to the bladder.
And after introduce the iron in the penis, perforating with ease until the perforator comes to that stone. And turn the perforator with your hand on that stone little by little, and you force the perforation of it until you make it penetrate from the other side; because the urine is immediately released.
And after press your hand over what remains of the stone from the outside part of the penis, because that is broken, and is thrown out with the urine, and the patient is healed.
But if this cure is not prepared for you for any cause which prohibits it, then tie a thread below the stone, and another thread above the stone. And after cut over the stone in that penis between two bindings. And after extract it. And after untie the binding and clean the congealed blood, which is made in the wound.
And it is not necessary to bind thread below the stone, except so that it does not return to the bladder, and the other binding above except, because when the thread is untied after the removal of the stone, the skin returns to its place and covers the wound.
And for this it is necessary for you when you tie the thread above, that you raise the skin to the parts above, or that it returns towards your completion, and covers the wound as we have said.
Chapter 61.
Of extraction of stone from women.
Stone in women is little engendered.

The third is because you do not find a woman well-knowing this art, especially the operation by hand.
And the fourth is that the place of the section over stone in women is far from the place of the stone, for which you need a deep section, and in that there is fear.
But if necessity provokes you to this, then it is fitting that you take a well-knowing female doctor, and little is found.
But if you are deprived of that, then seek a chaste and subtle doctor, or present a matron woman well-taught in the deed of women, or woman who in this art now part of the art.

But if she is not a virgin, then command the matron that she introduce her finger in the vagina of the patient and inquire about the stone, since she places her left hand over the bladder, and compress that with good compression.
So if she finds that, then it is fitting that she gradually move that from the orifice of the bladder to the parts below with the sum of her virtue until she comes with that to the root of the thigh.

And know that there are many types of stones: for of these there are small and large, and smooth and rough, and long and round, and having branches.
Therefore you should know how many types there are of it so that you can indicate which one you want.

And afterwards treat the wound.
Therefore when the acuteness of the blood has ceased after some days, and the place has healed, then you return to your operation until the stone is removed.
Chapter 62.
On the incision for watery hernia.
Watery hernia is nothing but an aggregation of moisture in the white membrane which is under the skin of the genitals containing the egg, and is called ciphac.
And sometimes it is in the proper membrane which nature prepared for it in the part of the egg, until it is thought that it is already another egg; and it is the skin of the genitals between the white membrane which we have mentioned, and this is not except rarely.
And the generation of this hernia is by weakness which happens to the genitals, for which this matter is poured into them, and sometimes it happens by percussion made on the genitals.
And this moisture has many colors, for its color is either inclining to citrine or to blood-like, or red, or it is black and feculent, or it is watery white, and this is what is most common.
And the signs by which it is known where this aggregation of water is are these: for if it is in the white membrane which we have mentioned, then the swelling is round inclining a little to length like the shape of an egg, and the genital appears, for the moisture contains it on all sides.
And if the moisture is in the proper membrane, then the swelling is round with part of the egg and for this reason one estimates that it is another egg.
And if the moisture is between the skin of the genitals and the white membrane, then it falls below the feeling.
And when you want knowledge of the color of the moisture, then you test the color of the moisture in the swelling with a square probe of which the form is preceded; and according to what has come out in the trace of the probe, judge what is inside it.
Therefore when we come to the cure of it with iron, then it is proper that we command the patient to be bled if this is possible for you, and you see his body full.
And afterwards let him be laid on his back on something a little high, and place many cloths under him.
And afterwards sit you on his left side, and command the assistant to sit on his right side, who extends his rod to one of two sides to the skin of the genitals and to the part of the mirac of the belly.
And afterwards take a broad spatula and cut the skin of the genitals from the middle place along the length until near the pubis.
And let the incision be made according to straightness equally distant from the line that divides the skin of the genitals, until it reaches the white containing membrane.
And flay it, and observe, and be careful not to cut it; and your flaying with which you flay it partially, even if it is suspended with the egg, but carefully examine with the flaying according to the quantity possible for you.
And then perforate the ciphac full of water with a wide perforation, and extract all the water.
And then separate between the two lips of the section with hooks, and extend the ciphac to the upper parts; and do not touch the skin comprising the genitals, and cut the ciphac in that manner which is possible for you. And cut it in its entirety or in pieces, and mainly its thin side, because if you do not examine carefully its incision, there is no guarantee that the water will not return.
But if the egg proceeds from that outside of its skin at the time of your operation, then when you have completed the section of the ciphac, return it inside, and then adjust the two lips of the skin of the genitals with suture, and then cure it as with other wounds, until it is healed.
And if you find the egg corrupted by another illness, then it is appropriate that you tie the vessels which are above the suspensory, and extract the egg, and then cure it with what we have said.
But if the water is gathered in two parts together, then know that there are two hernias; so cut that part as you have done in the other equally; and if it seems to you that it is one operation, then do it.
And then you clean the blood, and insert into the sections wool soaked in oil or rose oil; and place outside other wool which you have soaked in wine and oil, and spread it over the two genitals and the midriff of the belly; and place above doubled cloths and compresses, and tie those above with a bandage which is according to this form:
and then let two cloths be taken and filled with carded wool according to this likeness; and let the extremities be made with which it is pressed with cotton or wet wool, and let them be gathered with tightness in the fly of the trousers, and let one of the extremities take from the buttocks to the back, and the second take to the part of the groin, and two extremities over the two thighs below and two other extremities over the two groins, and let all tightness be adjusted in the fly of the trousers.
And sometimes this hernia is medicated artificially with cautery instead of section with iron; and it is that you take a subtle knife cautery and that you cut with it the skin of the genitals, and it is heated as we have recounted until the white ciphac containing the water is uncovered, and then you take a cautery according to this form: and it is resembling a Greek letter.
And then perforate with that ciphac, and it is heated until all the humidity is expelled.
And then extend the ciphac with hooks, and flay with hooks, and flay with subtle heated cautery; and cut it as is possible for you until you eradicate all of it; and be careful of the egg that the fire does not touch it.
And know that this operation is safer and further from blood flow, and better than operation with section.
But if it causes you difficulty, a hot abscess at the time of section or at the time of cautery, or blood flow, then it is appropriate that you cure whatever difficulty it causes you for this, with a cure which is suitable for it according to what is said.
But if the patient is fearful, and does not await the second operation due to its horribleness, then administer perforation according to what I recount here; and it is when it is certified by you, by what we have said of the signs, that this hernia is watery.
Then it is appropriate that you make the patient sit on some elevated seat, then pierce the abscess in the lowest part of it with a broad spatula, and make the perforation according to the length of the body.
And let the opening be wide until all the water flows out.
And then place cotton on the spot and bind it and leave it, so that the remaining water flows out. And then treat it until the wound is healed.
But if there is resistance to the discharge of the water at that time when you pierce it: and this is done only because the white membrane at the orifice of the wound causes resistance and prevents the exit of the water, then it is appropriate that you put in the wound a feather or instrument with which water is extracted from dropsy patients, the form of which precedes; or increase the pressure on the wound a little.
And know that the water returns, and is accumulated after six months or thereabouts; and when it is accumulated, then let it be pierced in that same manner, for the patient will thus pass his days.
Chapter 63.
On incision for fleshy hernia and its treatment.
Know that in the incision for this hernia there is fear leading to danger in most cases; therefore to me the dismissal of it and being saved by that seems better.
And I am recalling the operation on it and the types of abscesses.
So, I say that abscesses born in the bodies of which the genitals are composed and this is done for many reasons: either by sharp acrid superfluity, which is poured into the genitals, or by percussion.
And the color of the abscess is according to the color of the body, and pain is not found in it, and it is a severe abscess.
And very easily it is a petrified abscess, of which the color is dark, and there is no feeling in it.
And sometimes it is made by knotting of the arteries, and by inflation of those as has already been perceived the mention of it, or by inflation of veins.
But that which is by inflation of arteries is known by the dispersion of the abscess when you compress it with your fingers; and it is not appropriate that you touch that.
But that which is made by inflation of vein is not dispersed from it anything towards the compression with the fingers.
And it is already possible that on this type incision be made and on the other flesh; and it is that you cut the skin of the genitals, and then extend the egg to the upper parts, and extract it from the white membrane, and free the suspensory of the vessels, and tie them, and cut the suspensory after you free it from every part of the parts of the egg.
So if the egg is already consolidated with those fleshy parts, then it is appropriate that you extract the egg and cut it.
And if there is adherence to some part of the membrane, or between that which is between the vessels, then it is appropriate that you free all that adherence and cut it by round incision.
But if there is growth of flesh in the place of the adherence which is behind, then it is appropriate that you cut all that which is of it, and extract the egg as we have said.
So when your operation is completed, then fill the wound with wool soaked in rose oil and wine; and then treat it with the other treatment until it is healed.
Chapter 64.
On the treatment of hernia that is of the scrotum.
Scrotal hernia is a swelling wrapped by some covering similar to a bud with softening of the testicles, and it makes difficult exercise movement and walking for the patient.
And in the treatment of this disease there is fear because of which remembrance precedes.
However, it is appropriate that we speak of the operation on it according to what the ancients did.
And I say that it is appropriate that you make the patient sit on a raised chair; and then push the suspension of the testicles to the lower parts; and then hold the skin of the genitals with your fingers with the vessels that are close to the penis; and let another minister hold those than you, and extend them with vigorous extension.
And then incise with a wide sharp spatula by transverse section in the right of the vessels until the vessels are uncovered.
And then flay from every part as we have told you in the extraction of arteries which are in the temples.
And then stick in those a needle in which there is a double thread, and tie that in the first of the places in which the scrotum is affected, and tie that again in the last of them. And then incise those in the middle place by straight section according to the length of the body, and extract that which is gathered of foul and corrupt humors.
And then cure the wound with treatment of other wounds in which you want healing to be generated so that the vessels which nourish one of the two genitals fall, for it is not bad for that.
But if the scrotum affects all the vessels, then it is appropriate that the testicles be extracted or that the testicles for that dry up with the vessels, so that it is deprived of all nourishment by the incision of the vessels, and that they be destroyed, or that they dry up so that there is no benefit with them.
Chapter 65.
On the cure of intestinal hernia.
The advent of this hernia is by a cut that happens in the peritoneum extended over the belly from the part of the groins of the abdominal wall, through which the intestines descend from that rupture to some of the intestines.
And this rupture is either of the peritoneum or of extension of it, and these two species happen for many causes: either percussion, or by jumps, or by clamor, or by lifting of some heavy thing, or by similar things.
And the sign of that, when it is by extension of the peritoneum, is that it happens little by little over a long time, and does not happen suddenly, and is an even swelling down to the depth because the peritoneum compresses the intestine.
And the sign of it is when it is by cutting of the peritoneum, for at the beginning it makes violent pain happen suddenly; and it is a diverse swelling appearing under the nearby skin appearing, and that is by exit of the intestine, and the body of it to the outside parts of the peritoneum.
And sometimes the membrane is thrown out with the intestine, and this intestinal hernia is called omental.
And sometimes it is made with windiness, and sometimes a crack runs in the intestine, and there it is retained, and with that there is great danger for the patient, and sometimes it makes evil pain happen and especially when it is pressed.
And in the treatment of the types of this disease with iron there is fear, so it is advisable to avoid falling into it.
And the manner of operation for this is that you order the patient to reduce the intestine with his hand to the inner parts of his cavity if it obeys its return, and afterwards he is laid on his neck between your hands, and you raise his legs.
And then stretch the skin which follows the skin of the testicles to the upper parts, and cut the skin of the testicles all along the length; and then fix in two lips of the section hooks according to what you need to open the section with them.
And let the section be according to the quantity that is possible for you that from it the egg is thrown out.
And then skin that ciphaqueth which is below the skin of the testicles, until the white hard ciphac is uncovered on each side.
Then you insert your finger into what follows the testicle, into what is between white ciphac, which is under the skin of the egg, and between the second ciphac, and loosen with that adherence which is in the back part of the egg.
And then move with the hand the skin of the testicles to the outer parts, and with this extend the white ciphac upwards with the left hand, and raise the egg with the ciphac to the part of the section; and order the minister to extend the egg upwards and you dissolve the adherence that is behind with complete solution.
And search with your fingers that there is no cause of the intestine wrapped in the hard white ciphac. But if you find any cause of it, then you push it to the belly below.
And then cut in the lower part of the skin of the testicles by a section from which blood and pus run as we have recounted in what we have said.
And then administer wool submerged in oil, and place in the wound; and administer the binding which we have recounted (and sometimes the white ciphac is cauterized, which we have said after the cutting of it fearing blood flow, for many times it happens to them) and leave the binding until it falls by itself.
But if its falling is delayed, then let it be sprinkled with hot water, and place over it until it falls as we have said.
And then treat the wound with the other treatment of wounds until it is healed.
Chapter 66.
On windy hernia.
In this hernia I have not seen anyone who has been brave about treating it with iron.
And the first ones said that it is done as we have recounted in the hernia that is with wine; which is that you tie the vessels after the section over it with its ease; and then dry in the middle place around the abscess with what opens it, until the vessels fall.
And treat the wound as we have said until it is healed.
Chapter 67.
About the rupture that occurs in the groin.
Sometimes a rupture occurs in the groin as we have said, and the area swells.
And nothing from the intestines descends to the genitals; and if it does descend, it's very little; and it returns at all times.
But if the condition is prolonged, a fissure is added in the peritoneum until the intestine descends into the peritoneum; and this happens due to the extension of the peritoneum which is in the groin as we have said, which is because the peritoneum is stretched, and afterwards it softens and the area becomes swollen and protrudes.
And the cure for it is with cautery as has been previously narrated.
And sometimes it is cured with iron in this manner: the patient lies on his back between your hands, and then dry the area of the rupture of the swollen parts with an incision across the width of about three fingers.
And then tighten the white peritoneum that is under the skin until it is exposed.
And then take the probe and place it on the protruding part of the peritoneum, and press it into the depth of the belly.
And then sew the two protruding places over the end of the probe of the peritoneum, and join them together with sutures.
And then extract the end of the probe, and do not cut the peritoneum completely, nor extend the egg, nor anything else as I have informed you in the treatment of intestinal hernia.
And then treat it with the treatment for wounds, and when you cut the threads, clean it and restore the wound until it is healed; because the peritoneum is contracted and the protrusion of the rupture is not joined.
And cautery is better in this place, as it is closer to health.
Chapter 68.
About softening of the skin of the testicles.
Many times the skin of the testicles in some men is softened because the flesh between them is softened, and its appearance is ugly.
Then it is necessary for the one who is asked to cure it to make the patient lie on his back, and cut all the skin which is softened above the natural skin; and then join the two lips with sutures.
And if you want, sew at the beginning the excess of the softened skin with three or four stitches and with firm sutures.
And then cut between the sutures; and then treat it with the treatment for other wounds until it is healed and the threads fall out.
Chapter 69.
About castration.
Know that castration in our law is excommunicated, but for a reason it is allowed for me to remember it in this book; and the remembrance of it is only necessary for two reasons, of which one is so that it may be in the knowledge of the doctor when he is asked about it, that he may know the cure for one to whom it happens; and the other reason is that we often have need of castration of other animals for our benefit through them, such as rams, and goats, and pigs, and similar animals.
And so I say that castration is done in two ways: either by crushing, or by fissure or cutting.
But in that which is done by crushing, the way of the operation is that we make the animal sit in hot water until its genitals are softened and are slippery and hang down. And then take them with your hand until they are dissolved and do not appear under the touch.
But in castration done by fissure and cutting, it is necessary that you hold the animal and press the skin of its testicles with the left hand.
And then tie the suspensory, and cut over each egg with one cut until the two eggs come out.
And then cut them after you have skinned each one. And do not leave on them any of the peritoneum, except the thin peritoneum which is over the vessels.
And this manner of castration is better which is done by crushing, because crushing very easily leaves some of the testicles so that the animal desires coitus.
And then treat the wound until it is healed.
Chapter 70
On the treatment of hermaphroditism.
Hermaphroditism in men is of two types: one is when it appears in what follows the space in the skin of the testicles, in that which is between two testicles, resembling a woman's genitals in which there is hair.
And sometimes urine flows from that which is in the skin of the testicles.
But in women there is one type: and it is that the woman's genitals above the pubic area are like two male testicles, a little bit diminished on the outside part, like the foreskin of a man and two testicles.
And the treatment is of three types: two for men and one type for women. And it is that you should cut those joined flesh until the impression of it disappears, and afterwards treat those with the treatment of other wounds.
And in the second type of men from which urine flows, which is in the skin of the testicles, there is no treatment or operation for it.
Chapter 71
On lentigo and prominent flesh in women's parts.
Lentigo is easily added to natural parts until it is stretched and the appearance becomes ugly; and sometimes it is enlarged in some women so much that it is spread out as in men and reaches to coitus.
Then you should hold the excess of lentigo with your hand or with a hook and cut it.
And do not go too far in cutting, especially in the depth of the root, so that bleeding does not occur.
And afterwards treat it with the treatment of wounds until it is healed.
But grown flesh is flesh that grows in the orifice of the womb until it fills it, and it easily comes out to the outer parts in the shape of a tail (and for this reason some early [physicians] called this "tail disease"); therefore we should cut it as we cut lentigo, and treat it until it is healed.
Chapter 72
On the treatment of atresia.
Atresia is when the woman's genitals are not perforated, or the hole is small. And it is either natural or accidental.
Accidental is from a disease which has preceded, and that is made either by grown flesh added or by thin or thick membrane.
And it is made either in the depth of the womb, or in its sides, or in its uppermost part, or in its lowest part, and it prevents coitus and conception and childbirth, and often prevents menstruation.
And the diagnosis of it is made by the midwife's inspection, if the obstruction is apparent, nearby; but if it is not apparent, then you search for it with your fingers or with the probe.
But if the obstruction is by thin membrane, and is close to the two labia, then you hurry and break it.
And it is that you place pledgets on the two labia, and afterwards place your index fingers of both hands together.
And the woman should be on her back, her thighs extended, and afterwards extend the two labia forcefully until that thin membrane is broken and the obstruction is opened.
And afterwards take wool and soak it in oil and place it on the spot, and she should lie with a man that day so that the cut place does not heal.
But if the membrane is large and thick, then you should cut it with a broad spatula or with a myrtle leaf.
But if the obstruction is by grown flesh, then suspend it with a hook, and cut it.
And you should have with you medicines that stop bleeding without irritation, such as acacia, and dragon's blood, and incense, mixed with egg white.
And afterwards administer a wide lead cannula so that the wound does not heal too quickly.
And keep it for some days and administer dry flax tow.
And afterwards it should be treated with the other healing treatment until it is healed.
And sometimes other flesh growths occur in the womb, and then you should cut according to this method. But if this is due to a cancerous abscess, the cancerous abscess which is in the womb should not be opposed with iron in any way.
Chapter 73.
On the treatment of hemorrhoids and cuts and red swellings that occur in women's genitals.
Hemorrhoids are swellings of the orifices of many veins from which much blood flows continuously; and when hemorrhoids are old, they become cuts.
And I have already spoken in the division about their types and signs, and I will say here which ones can be cured and which ones cannot be cured.
Therefore I say that hemorrhoids and cuts when they are deep in the womb and not visible to the senses, then in those no treatment should be done with iron.
But those which are at the orifice of the womb, on which sensation falls, are those that are cured.
And it is appropriate that you put the woman in a warm house and afterwards extend the skin with scissors, or with rough cloth, and cut those at the roots.
And afterwards sprinkle over those where the blood flows one of the cutting powders without irritation, such as acacia and similar to those.
And afterwards raise her feet for an hour, and afterwards place her in cold water.
And if the blood flow persists, then make her sit in a decoction of sumac and pomegranate peels and galls and similar things.
And afterwards take barley flour and mix it with honey and vinegar and make a plaster with this on her back.
And if the blood is stopped, it is good; and if not, apply two cups to the breasts without scarification.
And afterwards take wool and submerge it in coriander juice or in plantain juice or in carob juice with diluted wine and apply to the place; and afterwards treat the place with ointments until it is healed.
And treat that until it is healed.
Chapter 74.
On perforation of an opening occurring in the womb.
Many types of swellings occur in the womb, such as cancer and stone-like swellings and ulcerations and adhesions and herpetic conditions and fistulas hemorrhoids and ragades and cuts and other swellings. And I have already spoken of these illnesses and their types and their signs, and their treatments in the division.
And it is appropriate that I speak in this treatise of hot swelling which comes in the womb when it is of the swellings that collect pus, and if you want to know in what manner the operation on it is done with iron.
Then it is appropriate that you consider if the pain of the swelling in its beginning is acute with percussion and phlegm and fever, and you see it redden and if sensation falls on it, then do not hurry with perforation of it, and treat it with that which helps with maturation until the acuteness of the symptoms ceases.
And then it is appropriate that you make the woman sit on a seat that has two seats; and recline on her back and bring her feet to the lower part of the belly, and her thighs should be spread, and place her arms under her knees, and tie each with a binding appropriate to this.
And afterwards the midwife should follow from the right side and administer the instrument with which the orifice of the womb is opened, the form of which will come in those things that will be done afterwards.
And it is appropriate when you want to administer this instrument that you insert with the probe the depth of the woman's womb, and that which of the instrument has entered the womb should not be more than the depth of the womb and injure the patient. But if the instrument is larger than the depth of the womb, then it is appropriate that you place pads on the texture of the depth of the womb so that the entry of the whole instrument into the depth of the womb is prevented.
It is necessary that you place the instrument on the upper side and that the minister holds the instrument and turns it until the orifice of the womb is opened.
And when the swelling appears, and is touched by hand and is smooth and soft, then it is necessary that you cut it towards the head with a wide spatula.
And when the blood is evacuated, then it is necessary that you place in the wound a wick soaked in rose oil or green oil in which there is some astringency; and place the compress in the incision in the depth of the womb.
And place outside the womb and over the pubic area clean wool soaked in water in which mallows have been boiled.
And afterwards it should be treated after two days with an ointment which is suitable for this until it is healed.
And sometimes the womb and the wound are washed so that it is treated with water and honey, and afterwards with water in which lily root or long aristolochia has been boiled, and afterwards return to the ointment.
And if the wound is hidden inside the womb, then it is necessary that you are prohibited from treating it with iron, having care for it with what we have said in the division.
Chapter 75.
To teach midwives in what manner living embryos should be treated when they come out in an unnatural position.
It is necessary that the midwife knows at the beginning the signs of natural childbirth, and it is that when you see the woman pushing in the lower parts and desiring to smell the air, and moreover is relieved by what is above her of the birth, and hastens the exit of the embryo, then know that this birth is according to natural position, and its exit is on its head, and the placenta with it or suspended or hanging from the navel.
Therefore when you see these signs, then it is necessary that her belly be compressed so that the embryo descends easily because when it descends on its head, the placenta descends to it, and it is cleansed of those superfluities with good cleansing.
But that which is other than this birth is unnatural and not praiseworthy, because when the embryo has come out on its feet and its body has come out before its head and its feet, and one of its hands, or to one of its feet, or its head has come out and its hand, or to its belly, and very easily it is turned on its neck, and similar to its undesirable positions.
Therefore it is necessary for the midwife to be wise and subtle in all these things, and to guard against error and deception.
And I am showing every position of these, and what skill is in these so that it may be signified by this and may have been upon this.
When the fetus has come out on its head by natural egress, and that is vehement on the woman and difficult birth is made to it, and you see its strength already weakened, then make her sit, or have the women hold her, and steam her vagina with cooked fenugreek and with moist oils.
And afterwards let the midwife introduce between her fingers a small spatula and split with it the placenta, or cut it with her nail until what is in it of moisture runs out. And press the woman's belly until the fetus descends.
But if it does not descend, then it is necessary that the woman be given an enema of psyllium mucilage and fenugreek mucilage with sesame.
And afterwards command her, after the enema, that she be compressed and make her sneeze with hellebore; and hold her mouth and her nose for an hour, because the fetus will be expelled soon.
And if the two hands of the fetus are expelled at the beginning, then it is necessary that you reduce them with a little facility little by little. But if it does not obey to enter, then place the woman on a chair and raise her feet up, and afterwards shake the chair on the ground; and the woman should be held so that she does not fall towards the shaking.
And if the hands are not turned inside and the fetus dies, then cut them and extract the remainder of the fetus or tie its body to its hand with a cloth and extract it with evenness, because it will be expelled.
When the fetus exits on its feet, then you should push those upwards, and then turn the small fetus, and then straighten it, and then take one of its feet and extend those little by little.
But when they have exited up to the thighs, then you command it to push, and make it sneeze with care, for it will be expelled if God wills it.
And if it is not expelled with what we have recounted, then you return the fetus little by little until you place it according to its natural position, for it will then be expelled with an easy exit.
And if it is prevented with all that we have recounted, then take marshmallow mucilage and dissolved gum, and pound all in the mortar with good pounding, and then anoint with this the woman's genitals, and the lower part of her belly. And then make her sit in lukewarm water, until it reaches the hypochondria.
And when you see that the parts below her are softened, then give her a fumigation of myrtle and place it under her. And when you have fumigated for an hour, then make her sit on a chair, and then make her sneeze and close her mouth, and lift her, and press the lower part of her belly with light compression, for the fetus will soon be expelled.
Exit of the fetus laterally with one of its hands hanging. Try to reduce its hand, but if you cannot reduce it, then lift the woman and make her walk.
And if she cannot walk, then make her lie on the bed, and shake her thighs with vigorous shaking, and then administer the bindings which I have recounted of mucilages.
And if childbirth has come, then make her sit on a chair, and then work on reducing the hand, and straighten the fetus according to its natural position, and make the woman sneeze and command her to push herself until it is expelled.
Exit of the fetus on its neck with its hands spread and its face to its mother's back. The midwife should hold the fetus's hand and then turn it little by little, and equalize it with ease.
And when it is and how much it is straightened, then place on her genitals what we have recounted of oil and mucilages.
And then command her to move little by little, and when you have done this, then make her sit on a chair and command her to be inclined on the right side, and then command her to push; and make her sneeze with care. Exit of the fetus prepared on its side.
When it descends to the mother's orifice in this manner, consider, and then you cut the afterbirth with your nail until it is evacuated of moisture.
And if the fetus is suspended on its face and neck, then you cut it from the navel, so that it is not retained and dies.
And then push the fetus to the inner parts until you place it as is appropriate, and order the woman to push herself several times, and it will be expelled with an easy exit, if God wills it.
Exit of twins or multiple fetuses. Know that twins are often born, and sometimes three or four are born, but this is strange and rarely happens; but five are unnatural, and do not live.
And count them, even if they are multiplied, as one pregnancy, and they are separated by the membrane, distinguishing them between the ligament in the navel of each one. And sometimes they are expelled as is one fetus by natural easy exit, and sometimes they are expelled by undesirable exit as we have recounted.
And if some of them are difficult during childbirth and come to what we have said of unnatural figures, then you cure them as we have recounted.
And let the midwife be subtle and do what she does with ease and subtlety, and with slowness, and be ingenious according to every figure as is prepared for her from the skill bringing to health.
Remembrance of what is formed in the womb from embryos and abortions.
Sometimes one, and two, and three, and four, and five, and six, and seven, and more than ten are formed in the mother, and it has been verified to me that a woman aborted and expelled six, and another ten all formed, which thing was done by measurement of the glorious wise men.
And all this should be in the knowledge of the midwife for it very easily appears similar to her, and thus opposes itself to that with what is appropriate.
Chapter 76.
On extraction of the fetus when it is dead.
When you cure the dead fetus with what we have said in the division of medication and it has not come out, and you are forced to use operation by hand, then it is appropriate that you consider if the woman is of sound virtue and is not with any of the accidents by which loss is feared over her.
Then it is appropriate that the woman be laid on the bed on her back, and let her head be inclined downwards and her thighs be elevated.
And the minister holds her from two parts or she is tied to the bed so that her body does not extend towards the extraction of the fetus.
And after you moisten the mouth of her womb with moist oils and with mucilage of marshmallow and fenugreek and linseed.
And after the midwife anoints her hand with those oils and mucilages, and after introduces her hand with ease into the womb, and after searches with the hand for a place in which to fix the hooks in the fetus.
And convenient places for this: then you consider if the fetus is prepared to descend on its head, and then you fix the hooks in its eyes, or in the neck, or in the mouth, or in the palate, or under the chin, or in its fork, or in the places near the ribs, or under the hypochondria.
But if the descent is over its feet, then in the pubic area, or in the middle of the ribs.
And it is appropriate that she hold the hook with the right hand, and place its curve in that place which is between the fingers of the left hand, and introduce the hand with ease and fix the hook in some of those places which we have said, until it reaches the empty thing.
And after place and fix in its apposition another hook, or the third if it is necessary, so that there is equal attraction, and there is not extension according to its straightness only.
Rather it is moved to every part, so that its exit is eased as is done in tooth towards its eradication.
And it is appropriate in it that which is between them that the extension be softened; and if some part of it is retained, then it is appropriate that the midwife anoint some of her fingers with oil and introduce them expertly and revolve with them that which is retained.
Thus if the part of the fetus is expelled, then the hooks are changed to a place which is higher; and do this until all the fetus is expelled.
But if the hand has come out before the other, and it is not possible to reduce it due to its constriction, then it is appropriate that cloth be wrapped over it; and after extract it until it is all expelled, and cut it either at the joint of the hand or at the elbow.
And so it is fitting that you do this with the other hand and with both feet.
But if the head of the fetus is large, or there is constriction during the exit, or there is water gathered in the head, then it is fitting to insert between the fingers a spiny spatula and split the head and extract the water, or to uncover it with an instrument which is called "alundat", the form of which will come with the forms of other instruments in the chapter which is after this one.
And similarly do if the fetus has a large head by nature: and then it is fitting to incise it with a scalpel, or to take it with the alunda as we have said; and afterwards extract the bones with forceps.
And if the head has exited and is constricted towards the clavicle, then let it be split until the fluid which is in the chest is poured out.
But if it is not complicated, nor obeys to exit, then you incise the head as soon as it will be possible for you.
And if the lower part of the belly is swollen or is in dropsy, then it is fitting that you perforate it until the fluid that is in it runs out.
But if the fetus is on its feet, then the attraction of it is easy and the direction of it to the mouth of the womb is easy.
But if it is constricted towards the belly and chest, then it is fitting that you extract it with a cloth which you will have wrapped over your hand, and that you split the belly and chest until that which is in them runs out.
